<p><b>Game of the Year</b> (abbreviated <b>GotY</b>) is a title awarded by various <a href="/wiki/Video_game_journalism" title="Video game journalism">gaming publications</a> to a deserving <a href="/wiki/Game" title="Game">game</a>. Many publications award a single "Game of the Year" to a single title that they feel represents the pinnacle of gaming achievement that year. Many games will release a "Game of the Year" edition after winning any of these awards, usually containing all the updates, <a href="/wiki/Downloadable_content" title="Downloadable content">downloadable content</a> (DLC) and occasionally other extras such as a <a href="/wiki/Soundtrack" title="Soundtrack">soundtrack</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1UP.com">1UP.com</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: 1UP.com">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the winners of 1UP's Game of the Year are chosen by the editors. (In 2009, they also revealed their picks in the Reader's Choice Awards). For the Reader's Choice, see the <a href="#Video_games_.E2.80.93_Reader_and_gamer_polls">Reader and gamer polls</a> GOTY Section below.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1UP.com_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-1UP.com-1">[1]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Readers_choice">Readers choice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Readers choice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Academy_Games_Awards_.28Formerly:_BAFTA_Interactive_Entertainment_Awards.29">British Academy Games Awards (Formerly: BAFTA Interactive Entertainment Awards)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: British Academy Games Awards (Formerly: BAFTA Interactive Entertainment Awards)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Games_Awards" title="British Academy Games Awards">British Academy Games Awards</a> are an annual British awards ceremony honoring "outstanding creative achievement" in the video game industry. First presented in 2004 following the restructuring of the <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Interactive_Entertainment_Awards" title="BAFTA Interactive Entertainment Awards">BAFTA Interactive Entertainment Awards</a>, the awards are presented by the British Academy of Film and Television Arts (BAFTA), and are thus commonly referred to as the BAFTA Games Awards.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="CGR">CGR</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: CGR">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The CGR Awards include 3 different awards for each category: the community's pick, staff's pick and host's pick.</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<th>Year</th>
<th>Game</th>
<th>Genre</th>
<th>Platform(s)</th>
<th>Developer(s)</th>
</tr>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Crash">Crash</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Crash">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="D.I.C.E._Awards_.28Formerly:_Academy_of_Interactive_Arts_.26_Sciences.29">D.I.C.E. Awards (Formerly: Academy of Interactive Arts &amp; Sciences)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: D.I.C.E. Awards (Formerly: Academy of Interactive Arts &amp; Sciences)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Interactive_Arts_%26_Sciences" title="Academy of Interactive Arts &amp; Sciences">Academy of Interactive Arts &amp; Sciences (AIAS)</a> is a non-profit organization of industry professionals and presents a series of annual Interactive Achievement Awards. On October 24, 2012, the Academy of Interactive Arts &amp; Sciences announced that the IAAs would be known as the D.I.C.E. Awards beginning in 2013. The name stands for "Design, Innovate, Communicate, Entertain".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Easy_Allies_.28Formerly:_GameTrailers.29">Easy Allies (Formerly: GameTrailers)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Easy Allies (Formerly: GameTrailers)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Electronic_Games"><i>Electronic Games</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Electronic Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Along with the Arcade Awards announced by <i><a href="/wiki/Electronic_Games" title="Electronic Games">Electronic Games</a></i> magazine each year, it also held a regular reader poll for the most popular games among its readers in each issue, from May 1982 to January 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eg_archive_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-eg_archive-73">[73]</a></sup> The games that topped these polls the most in each year are listed here.</p>

<th><a href="/wiki/PC_game" title="PC game">Computer</a></th>
</tr>
<tr>

<td><i><a href="/wiki/Pac-Man" title="Pac-Man">Pac-Man</a></i></td>
<td><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pac-Man_(Atari_2600)" title="Pac-Man (Atari 2600)">Pac-Man</a></i></td>
<td rowspan="2"><i><a href="/wiki/Star_Raiders" title="Star Raiders">Star Raiders</a></i></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1983</td>
<td><i><a href="/wiki/Pole_Position_(video_game)" title="Pole Position (video game)">Pole Position</a></i></td>
<td><i><a href="/wiki/Donkey_Kong_(video_game)" title="Donkey Kong (video game)">Donkey Kong</a></i><br/>

</tr>

<td><i><a href="/wiki/Donkey_Kong_Jr." title="Donkey Kong Jr.">Donkey Kong Jr.</a></i><br/>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Electronic_Gaming_Awards_.28Formerly:_Arcade_Awards.29">Electronic Gaming Awards (Formerly: Arcade Awards)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Electronic Gaming Awards (Formerly: Arcade Awards)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Arcade Awards, also known as the Arkie Awards, was one of the first video game awards, dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Golden_age_of_arcade_video_games" title="Golden age of arcade video games">golden age of arcade video games</a> and lasting up until the <a href="/wiki/North_American_video_game_crash_of_1983" title="North American video game crash of 1983">North American video game industry crash</a>. It was held since 1980 (for games released in 1979 and earlier) and were announced annually by <i><a href="/wiki/Electronic_Games" title="Electronic Games">Electronic Games</a></i> magazine since 1981, covering several different platform categories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eg_archive_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-eg_archive-73">[73]</a></sup> Following the magazine's revival in 1992, it published the Electronic Gaming Awards in January 1993 for the best video games released in 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The 1992 and 1993 issues asked their readers to vote for the game of the year.</p>

<th><a href="/wiki/Dedicated_console" title="Dedicated console">Standalone</a></th>
<th><a href="/wiki/Console_game" title="Console game">Console</a></th>
<th><a href="/wiki/PC_game" title="PC game">Computer</a></th>
</tr>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Electronic_Gaming_Monthly"><i>Electronic Gaming Monthly</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Electronic Gaming Monthly">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Famitsu_Awards"><i>Famitsu</i> Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Famitsu Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Game_Awards_.28Formerly:_Spike_Video_Game_Awards.29">The Game Awards (Formerly: Spike Video Game Awards)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: The Game Awards (Formerly: Spike Video Game Awards)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The winners of the <a href="/wiki/Spike_Video_Game_Awards" title="Spike Video Game Awards">Spike Video Game Awards</a>, hosted by <a href="/wiki/Spike_(TV_network)" title="Spike (TV network)">Spike</a> between 2003 and 2013, awarded the Game of the Year using an advisory council featuring over 20 journalists from media outlets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> The show's title was changed to VGX in 2013 before Spike TV dropped the show entirely. It was replaced by <a href="/wiki/The_Game_Awards" title="The Game Awards">The Game Awards</a> in 2014.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_Developers_Choice_Awards">Game Developers Choice Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Game Developers Choice Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_Informer"><i>Game Informer</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Game Informer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The winners of the <i><a href="/wiki/Game_Informer" title="Game Informer">Game Informer</a></i> Game of the Year are chosen by Game Informer editors. During their first years of publication they would give awards for the best game on each console available at the time, occasionally giving an award to the overall best game of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_Revolution"><i>Game Revolution</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Game Revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The winner of the <i><a href="/wiki/Game_Revolution" title="Game Revolution">Game Revolution</a></i> Community Choice Game of the Year award, but in 2013 the editors chose the Game of the Year.</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="GamePro"><i>GamePro</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: GamePro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The winners of the <i><a href="/wiki/GamePro" title="GamePro">GamePro</a></i> Game of the Year are chosen by <i>GamePro</i> editors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> In the 1990s, the winners were chosen by editors from 1993<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> to 1995,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> and by readers for 1991,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> 1992,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> 1996,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> 1997<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> and 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> Since 2011, the winners of GamePro Game of the Year are chosen by <a href="/wiki/GamePro_TV" title="GamePro TV">GamePro TV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<th>Year</th>
<th><a href="/wiki/Arcade_game" title="Arcade game">Arcade</a></th>
<th><a href="/wiki/Console_game" title="Console game">Console</a></th>
<th><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Handheld_game" title="Handheld game">Handheld</a></th>
</tr>

<td><i><a href="/wiki/Mega_Man:_Dr._Wily%27s_Revenge" title="Mega Man: Dr. Wily's Revenge">Mega Man</a></i> (Game Boy)</td>
</tr>

<a href="/wiki/Sega_Genesis" title="Sega Genesis">Sega Genesis</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/Disney%27s_Aladdin_(Virgin_Games)" title="Disney's Aladdin (Virgin Games)">Disney's Aladdin</a></i><br/>

<td>1995</td>
<td>Arcade: <i><a href="/wiki/Tekken_2" title="Tekken 2">Tekken 2</a></i><br/>
<a href="/wiki/Neo_Geo_(system)" title="Neo Geo (system)">Neo Geo</a>: <i><a href="/wiki/World_Heroes_Perfect" title="World Heroes Perfect">World Heroes Perfect</a></i></td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="GameRankings">GameRankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: GameRankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Games"><i>Games</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The winners of the <a href="/wiki/Games_(magazine)" title="Games (magazine)"><i>Games</i> magazine</a> Game of the Year award are chosen by <i>Games</i> editors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> Electronic games are covered separately on the publication's annual <a href="/wiki/Games_100" title="Games 100">Games 100</a> list.</p>

<ul>
<li>Starting in 1996, awards were given the title of the coming year (e.g. <i>The Sims</i> was named <i>Game of the Year 2001</i>, despite being released in 2000). Thus, the December 1995 issue awarded the "Game of the Year 1995", whereas the December 1996 issue awarded the "Game of the Year 1997".</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gamest_Awards"><i>Gamest</i> Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Gamest Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Japanese <i><a class="extiw" href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamest" title="jp:Gamest">Gamest</a></i> magazine was published from 1986 to 1999, and held the <a class="extiw" href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E3%82%B2%E3%83%BC%E3%83%A1%E3%82%B9%E3%83%88%E5%A4%A7%E8%B3%9E" title="jp:ゲーメスト大賞"><i>Gamest</i> Award</a> ceremonies every year, focusing exclusively on <a href="/wiki/Arcade_game" title="Arcade game">arcade games</a>. The winners of the Grand Prize awards were chosen by voters.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Golden_Joystick_Awards">Golden Joystick Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Golden Joystick Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Joystick_Award" title="Golden Joystick Award">Golden Joystick Awards</a> is the second oldest gaming award ceremony and is the longest running video game award. The inaugural ceremony took place in 1984 in London's <a href="/wiki/Berkeley_Square" title="Berkeley Square">Berkeley Square</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2014, it is the biggest video game award show in terms of the number of votes cast; over nine million votes were cast for the 2014 ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<th>Year</th>
<th>Game</th>
<th>Genre</th>
<th>Platform(s)</th>
<th>Developer(s)</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1983</td>
<td><i><a href="/wiki/Jetpac" title="Jetpac">Jetpac</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GamesRadar_Joystick_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-GamesRadar_Joystick-249">[249]</a></sup></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Shooter_game" title="Shooter game">Shooter</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Commodore_VIC-20" title="Commodore VIC-20">Commodore VIC-20</a>, <a href="/wiki/ZX_Spectrum" title="ZX Spectrum">ZX Spectrum</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Play_the_Game" title="Ultimate Play the Game">Ultimate</a></td>
</tr>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="IGN">IGN</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: IGN">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a>'s game of the year award is chosen by all the editors at IGN and are announced mid-January.</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<th>Year</th>
<th>Game</th>
<th>Genre</th>
<th>Platform(s)</th>
<th>Developer(s)</th>

<td>2001</td>
<td><i><a href="/wiki/Halo:_Combat_Evolved" title="Halo: Combat Evolved">Halo: Combat Evolved</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/First-person_shooter" title="First-person shooter">First-person shooter</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Xbox_(console)" title="Xbox (console)">Xbox</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Bungie" title="Bungie">Bungie</a></td>
</tr>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Readers_choice_5">Readers choice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Readers choice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Inside_Gaming_Awards">Inside Gaming Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Inside Gaming Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Machinima_Inc." title="Machinima Inc.">Machinima</a> also hosts its own awards show, the <i>Inside Gaming Awards</i>, annually in Los Angeles. The awards show celebrates the biggest developers and achievements in the video-games industry, and features top gaming choices by viewers and the staff of Inside Gaming.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan_Game_Awards_.28Formerly:_CESA_Awards.29">Japan Game Awards (Formerly: CESA Awards)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Japan Game Awards (Formerly: CESA Awards)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The winners of the Grand Award annually given by the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Game_Awards" title="Japan Game Awards">Japan Game Awards</a>, formerly known as the CESA Awards, since 1996. There are some years where two games shared the Grand Award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tr>
<th>Year</th>
<th>Game</th>
<th>Genre</th>
<th>Platform(s)</th>
<th>Developer(s)</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>1996</td>
<td><i><a href="/wiki/Sakura_Wars" title="Sakura Wars">Sakura Wars</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Tactical_role-playing_game" title="Tactical role-playing game">Tactical RPG</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dating_sim" title="Dating sim">Dating Sim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visual_novel" title="Visual novel">Visual Novel</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Sega_Saturn" title="Sega Saturn">Sega Saturn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dreamcast" title="Dreamcast">Dreamcast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Windows</a>, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a>, <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Portable" title="PlayStation Portable">PlayStation Portable</a>, <a href="/wiki/I-mode" title="I-mode">i-mode</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Sega" title="Sega">Sega</a></td>
</tr>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Kotaku">Kotaku</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Kotaku">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Over the years, <a href="/wiki/Kotaku" title="Kotaku">Kotaku</a> has been refining how it selects its Game of the Year. Currently, it involves a debate which starts with the Kotaku editors determining the four most defendable candidates for the award. Editors are then given time to play all the games, and for each of the candidates, an appropriate editor is determined to make his case behind it in front of a panel who also raise questions. The results of these debates are given to the readers, who then also have the chance to make their own opinions felt. To make the final decision, the Kotaku staff members reexamine their arguments, and the winner is determined from a vote between the editors in late January.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Metacritic">Metacritic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Metacritic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The winners of the <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a> Game of the Year are determined by the game with the highest score garnered from an average of weighted review scores from various sources. Each year, Metacritic announce the highest in an official award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metacritic_301-0"><a href="#cite_note-Metacritic-301">[301]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="MMGN">MMGN</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: MMGN">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=MMGN&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="MMGN (page does not exist)">MMGN</a>'s annual Community Game of the Year poll is 100% community driven. The semi-finals allow registered members to choose up to three games for each genre, and award up to nine points across the three games, but no more than 5 points for one game. The top 5 games from each genre with the most points are then added to final polls, where each member gets one vote per genre.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="NAVGTR_Awards">NAVGTR Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: NAVGTR Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="X-Play"><i>X-Play</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Game_of_the_Year_awards&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: X-Play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The winners of the <i><a href="/wiki/X-Play" title="X-Play">X-Play</a></i> Game of the Year were chosen by <i>X-Play</i> editors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-351"><a href="#cite_note-351">[351]</a></sup> The show ended in January 2013.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Yahoo.21_Games"><i>Yahoo! Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
